It can define protection for threatened ecosystems, but also some rights and duties (for example, <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a> and hunting rights).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>Law regarding species is more recent. It defines species that must be protected because they may be threatened by extinction. The U.S. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endangered_Species_Act" title="Endangered Species Act">Endangered Species Act</a> is an example of an attempt to address the "law and species" issue.</li>
<li>Laws regarding gene pools are only about a century old.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Domestication and plant breeding methods are not new, but advances in genetic engineering have led to tighter laws covering distribution of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genetically_modified_organisms" title="Genetically modified organisms">genetically modified organisms</a>, gene <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patents</a> and process patents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> Governments struggle to decide whether to focus on for example, genes, genomes, or organisms and species.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li></ul>
<p>Uniform approval for use of biodiversity as a legal standard has not been achieved, however. Bosselman argues that biodiversity should not be used as a legal standard, claiming that the remaining areas of scientific uncertainty cause unacceptable administrative waste and increase litigation without promoting preservation goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup>
</p><p>India passed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_Diversity_Act" title="Biological Diversity Act">Biological Diversity Act</a> in 2002 for the conservation of biological diversity in India. The Act also provides mechanisms for equitable sharing of benefits from the use of traditional biological resources and knowledge.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Analytical_limits">Analytical limits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Analytical limits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxonomic_and_size_relationships">Taxonomic and size relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Taxonomic and size relationships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Less than 1% of all species that have been described have been studied beyond simply noting their existence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> The vast majority of Earth's species are microbial. Contemporary biodiversity physics is "firmly fixated on the visible [macroscopic] world".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> For example, microbial life is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metabolically" title="Metabolically">metabolically</a> and environmentally more diverse than multicellular life (see e.g., <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">extremophile</a>). "On the tree of life, based on analyses of small-subunit <a href="/wiki/Ribosomal_RNA" title="Ribosomal RNA">ribosomal RNA</a>, visible life consists of barely noticeable twigs. The inverse relationship of size and population recurs higher on the evolutionary ladder—to a first approximation, all multicellular species on Earth are insects".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> Insect extinction rates are high—supporting the Holocene extinction hypothesis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Diversity_study_.28botany.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Diversity_study_(botany)">Diversity study (botany)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Diversity study (botany)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The number of morphological attributes that can be scored for diversity study is generally limited and prone to environmental influences; thereby reducing the fine resolution required to ascertain the phylogenetic relationships. DNA based markers- microsatellites otherwise known as <i>simple sequence repeats</i> (SSR) were therefore used for the diversity studies of certain species and their wild relatives.
</p><p>In the case of <a href="/wiki/Cowpea" title="Cowpea">cowpea</a>, a study conducted to assess the level of genetic diversity in cowpea germplasm and related wide species, where the relatedness among various taxa were compared, primers useful for classification of taxa identified, and the origin and phylogeny of cultivated cowpea classified show that SSR markers are useful in validating with species classification and revealing the center of diversity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tools">Tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a class="external text" href="http://www.globio.info/" rel="nofollow">GLOBIO</a>, an ongoing programme to map the past, current and future impacts of human activities on biodiversity</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20050825002841/http://stort.unep-wcmc.org/imaps/gb2002/book/viewer.htm" rel="nofollow">World Map of Biodiversity</a> an interactive map from the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Conservation_Monitoring_Centre" title="World Conservation Monitoring Centre">World Conservation Monitoring Centre</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://bison.usgs.gov/#home" rel="nofollow">Biodiversity Information Serving Our Nation (BISON)</a>, provides a United States gateway for serving, searching, mapping and downloading integrated species occurrence records from multiple data sources</li></ul>
